ووقف دابة هي راكبتها لا يقطع، وفلكها كبيتها، وسير دابتها كسيرها، وفي اختاري لا تصح نية الثلاث [١] قوله: ووقف دابة؛ أي سكونها وامتناعها عن السير أو إسكانها ومنعها عن السير. [٢] قوله: لا يقطع؛ فإنّ هذه الأمور ليس فيها تبدل حقيقة ولا حكماً؛ لعدم دلالتها على الإعراض، فلو كانت قائمة فجلست فهي على خيارها؛ لأنه دليل الإقبال؛ فإنّ القعود أجمع للرأي، وكذا إذا كانت قاعدة فاتكأت بالوسادة، أو متكئة فقعدت وهجرت الوسادة؛ لأنه انتقال من جلسة إلى جلسة، فلا يدل على الإعراض. وكذا طلب الأب للشورى أو الشهود للإشهاد ليس دليلاً على الإعراض، بل هو لتحري الصواب والتحرز عن الإنكار، وكذا سكون مركوبها، بخلاف سيرها، فإنّ سير الدابة ووقوفها مضاف إليها، فوقوفها في حكم وقوفها، فلا يكون دليلاً على الإعراض، وسيرها كمشيها، هو دليل على الإعراض. [٣] قوله: وفلكها؛ بضم الفاء -: هي السفينة الجارية في البحر أو الساكنة على الشط، وكونه في حكم البيتِ أنه لا يبطل الخيار بانتقالها من جانب إلى جانب منه، ولا تعتبر حركة السفينة؛ لأنه ليس باختيار الراكب، فلا تضاف إليه، بخلاف الدابة، فإنّه يقدر على إيقافه وتسييره. وفي حكم الفلك المركب الدخاني الذي يسير بالمسافرين على الأرض بقوة الدخان، كما أنه في حكمه في حق جواز الصلاة فيه حالة سكونه وحركته، وفي وجوب استدارة المصلِّي إلى القبلة لو اختلفت الجهة بسيرها. [٤] قوله: لا تصح نية الثلاث؛ علله صاحب «الهداية» بأنّ الاختيار لا يتنوّع. راكبتها بمنزلة بيتها لأن جريان السفينة لا يضاف إلى راكبها، ولهذا لا يقدر
And the stopping of an animal that she is riding does not cut it, and her ship is like her house, and the walking of her animal is like her walking, and in 'I choose' the intention of three is not valid. [1] His statement: 'and the stopping of an animal'; i.e., its stillness and its refraining from walking, or its being made to stop and prevented from walking. [2] His statement: 'does not cut'; for these matters have no actual or legal change in them, due to the lack of indication of disinterest. So if she was standing and then sat down, she is still upon her option, because it is an indication of inclination, for sitting is more collected for opinion. Similarly, if she was sitting and then leaned on a cushion, or leaning and then sat down and abandoned the cushion, because it is a transition from one sitting to another, so it does not indicate disinterest. Similarly, the father's request for consultation or the witnesses for witnessing is not evidence of disinterest, rather it is for seeking correctness and guarding against denial. Similarly, the stillness of her mount, unlike its walking, for the walking and stopping of the animal are attributed to her, so its stopping is in the ruling of her stopping, so it is not evidence of disinterest, whereas its walking is like her walking, it is evidence of disinterest. [3] His statement: 'and her ship' (with dammah on the fa): it is the ship sailing in the sea or stationary on the shore, and its being in the ruling of the house is that the option is not invalidated by her moving from one side to another within it, and the movement of the ship is not considered because it is not by the rider's choice, so it is not attributed to her, unlike the animal, for she can stop it and make it walk. And in the ruling of the ship is the steamship that travels with passengers on land by the power of steam, just as it is in the ruling regarding the permissibility of praying in it while stationary and moving, and regarding the obligation of the worshipper turning towards the qibla if the direction changes by its travel. [4] His statement: 'the intention of three is not valid'; the author of al-Hidayah explained it by saying that choice (ikhtiyar) is not divisible (into types). Her riding it is like her house because the sailing of the ship is not attributed to its rider, and therefore she cannot.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn from Al-Wiqayah, focusing on the effects of a woman's mount and ship on her option in delegated divorce, and the ruling on intending three divorces when saying 'I choose myself.' The author explains that stopping an animal she rides does not cut the option because it is not an action indicating disinterest; it is akin to the woman's own stillness. Similarly, her ship is like her house: moving within it does not change the session, and the ship's motion is not attributed to her, so it does not nullify the option. However, if the animal walks, it is like her walking, so that would indicate disinterest and nullify the option. A ship is different because the rider has no control over its movement. The commentary also mentions steamships in an analogy for prayer rulings. Finally, the author addresses the issue of intention: if the woman says 'I choose myself' intending three divorces, the intention is not valid and only one divorce occurs. The reason is that choice (ikhtiyar) is not divisible; the word 'choose' inherently refers to a single action, so it cannot be used to effect multiple divorces at once. This is the held position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الفلك (al-fulk): Ship or vessel that travels on sea or river, considered like the rider's house for the purpose of the option.
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyar): The word 'I choose' used by the wife in delegated divorce to accept the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a woman given the choice for divorce says 'I choose myself' with the intention of divorcing three times?
A) Three divorces take effect because she intended them.
B) One divorce takes effect because intention does not increase the number.
C) No divorce takes effect because the utterance is ambiguous.
D) The divorce is invalid due to lack of clarity.

Key Takeaway
In delegated divorce, only the woman's own actions indicating disinterest nullify the option, and the word 'I choose' cannot effect more than one divorce.
